Indy

Accountability in Action for the City of Indianapolis

Date:

September 11, 2008

To:

Mayor Ballard

From: Michael Huber and Kristen Tusing, Office of Enterprise Development
Re:

IndyStat –Neighborhoods meeting Friday 9/12/08

CC:

Olgen Williams, Deputy Mayor of Neighborhoods
Paul Okeson, Chief of Staff
Sarah Taylor, Director of Constituent Services
David Reynolds, Controller
Chris Cotterill, Corporation Counsel
Kevin Ortell, Interim Chief Information Officer

The following issues were highlighted in the July 11th and August 8th meeting and appeared in the
Neighborhoods IndyStat follow-up memo:
Re-entry
Follow-up Action. Create a detailed timeline of when the future measures will be created and
collected.
How will data be collected? Who will we need to partner with to obtain the data? How will
the measures specific define how well the Initiative is working? By what date will we be
ready to report re-entry performance measures on a regular basis?
Front Porch Alliance
Follow-up Action. Are there established criteria for being part of the Front Porch Alliance?
Provide a timeline for information collection to be mainly complete. Provide information
regarding what type of Federal funding has the community received. What other funding
besides government funding is appropriate to assist community is receiving?
Can we use the “Front Porch Alliance designation” as an incentive for organizations to provide
program information (i.e., you may become a member of the Alliance provided you update the
City on your programs and capabilities). Would it be beneficial to form a Front Porch
Alliance committee to gain assistance in information needed?
Abandoned Homes
Follow-up Action. Provide the status of the IT function of collecting data and tracking it
continually.
What are the plans of action for each of the categories identified through the Abandoned
Homes data match project? Who should the City work with? What changes are needed in
enforcement?
Provide geographical maps to show where properties are located.

1

Comprehensive Anti-Gang Initiative and COIT
Follow-up Action. Provide status update on grantee process. Provide outcome numbers collected
from grantees.

Potential Issues for Discussion
•

How do we designate a “connected organization” of the Front Porch Alliance? How does an
organization become connected?

•

Where are the performance measures or baseline data for Front Porch Alliance?

•

What does the relationship between selected churches and IMPD beats tell us? How are
churches selected as partners in the initiative?

•

What is the Anti-Gang Initiative?

•

How will the funds be distributed? Who will be the recipients?

•

What data will grantees be required to report back to the City to be in compliance of the
funds issued?

•

What actions are already being taken regarding abandoned homes? How can we measure the
City’s ability to act fast?

•

What is the cost associated with an abandoned home?

•

Is the relationship between demolition permits and Utilities Disconnects helpful? What does
the information tell us?

•

What is the role the City will play in facilitating the re-entry of its offenders?

•

Describe how ex-offenders will be tracked after they leave incarceration.

•

Current data on offenders released to the community displays a higher concentration of
offenders in the central and east side of the cities. How does this impact the focus of the reentry initiative?

•

How is the statistical data used to improve the re-entry initiative? What performance
measures help the City understand whether its re-entry efforts have been successful?

•

What road blocks have been found to improve the re-entry focus of the City? What
relationships have been formed or need to be formed to improve the initiative?

2

Transitional: Unoccupied privately-owned housing in the normal market process
of being for sale, for rent, rehabilitation, in probate, or foreclosure.
Distressed: Privately-owned housing that has become vacant, or well into the
process of becoming vacant. These units are most likely in violation of
zoning/health codes and many are tax delinquent.
Abandoned: Housing that remains un-purchased and unredeemed after the
County tax sale and has come under the ownership of the County.

Indy

The Community Crime
Prevention Grant $5M (COIT)

Stat

Accountability in Action for the City of Indianapolis





A total of 381 people attended the two TA Sessions.
Deadline for proposals was extended from September 8th to
September 22nd
This conclusion was reached based upon several indicators:
a) TA attendees exceeded the Fire Marshal’s occupancy number at
the morning session. Approximately, 50 people were forced to
stand through the training because they refused to leave and the
IMPD North District facility ran out of available chairs. Another 40
individuals left their contact information, but was unable to stay.
b) To provide further clarity regarding the budget, allowable
expenses and payment schedule of funds.
c) To allow applicants sufficient time to finish their proposals and
secure their letters of collaboration and support.

September 12, 2008

Indy

Accountability in Action for the City of Indianapolis

Date:

September 15, 2008

To:

Olgen Williams, Deputy Mayor of Neighborhoods

From: Michael Huber and Kristen Tusing, Office of Enterprise Development
Re:

Follow-up to Neighborhoods IndyStat Meeting held September 12, 2008

Cc:

Mayor Greg Ballard
Paul Okeson, Chief of Staff
David Reynolds, Controller
Chris Cotterill, Corporation Counsel
Sarah Taylor, Constituent Services
Kevin Ortell, Interim Chief Information Officer

The following follow-ups will be for the October 10th Neighborhoods IndyStat meeting.

Front Porch Alliance
Follow-up Action. We lack performance measures for the Front Porch Alliance other than
Federal funds received. Create performance measures for the Alliance by October 3, 2008.
Are there established criteria for being part of the Front Porch Alliance? Provide a timeline for
information collection to be mainly complete. Provide information regarding what type of Federal
funding has the community received. What other funding besides government funding is
appropriate to assist community is receiving? (If Federal funding does not meet the Alliance’s
performance measures, pursuing this funding should not be considered core to the Alliance’s
mission.)
Should we use the “Front Porch Alliance designation” as an incentive for organizations to provide
program information (i.e., you may become a member of the Alliance provided you update the
City on your programs and capabilities). Would it be beneficial to form a Front Porch Alliance
committee to gain assistance in information needed?
Comprehensive Anti-Gang Initiative and COIT
Follow-up Action. Provide status update on grantee process. Provide outcome numbers collected
from grantees.
Neighborhood Liaisons
Follow-up Action. Provide an overview of the Mayor’s Neighborhood Liaison (MNL) functions.
What are the strategic (measurable) goals of the MNL’s?
How is MNL activity measured? What outcomes drive MNL performance?

1

The following follow-ups will be discussed in the November 14th Neighborhoods meeting.
Re-entry
Follow-up Action. Provide benchmarks for re-entry for the end of the year. How will we know
that we as an administration have had a positive impact on ex-offenders released to the
community? If we concentrate on employment, what are the key performance indicators for the
initiative? How will this data be collected?
Should we explore financial incentives to provide to employers that hire and retain offenders?
How would the city encourage the program? What would need to be changed in law and
ordinance? Would there be state support for the initiative?
Provide information on health care grants available for ex-offenders. Where are the gapsin care?
What other tools does the Administration have at its disposal?
Abandoned Homes
Follow-up Action. Provide update on Abandoned House task force meeting.
Update the panel on work being done with ISA to automate data collection process.
What actions can be taken to reduce vacant homes? What outcomes can we account for?

2
